Expansion Plan

  • Establish quality bar: fairness, pacing, clarity, and consistency.

How to Use This Book

Deep read once, quick‑reference forever. Start with Gameplay Philosophy and The Gameplay Loop to absorb the system’s rhythm; then jump to Scene & Encounter Structure for the procedure you’ll use every session. Combat (GM Guidance) provides an at‑table flow with micro‑checklists and examples. Mechanics Overview (GM) summarizes must‑know levers (DCs, tiers, tags/conditions, clocks). Worked Examples show fully annotated scenes; Quick References compile the most‑used tables and checklists. Cross‑links point to Player, Storyteller, and Mechanics books when you need alternate angles or deeper catalogs.

Pointer: For live play, keep Quick Reference Sheets open alongside this chapter. They condense DC cues, tiers, the loop/scene steps, tags/conditions, group checks/contests, combat actions, and a rulings checklist.

What This Book Is Not

  • Not lore: this is a practical GM guide, not setting fiction.
  • Not a rules compendium: technical rules scaffolding was transformed into accessible, fiction-first guidance here.
  • Not exhaustive catalogs: we link to references instead of duplicating them.

Audience & Goals

Who this serves: (1) New GMs learning this system; (2) Experienced GMs translating their instincts to these tools. Outcomes: you can frame compelling scenes in minutes, adjudicate checks confidently, keep tension rising and falling on purpose, and explain outcomes so players trust the world—even when the dice complicate things. You’ll also know how to prep efficiently, compose enemies and threats, and finish sessions with clear momentum for next time.

Structure of the Guide

  • Gameplay Philosophy: the values that shape rulings and pacing.
  • The Gameplay Loop: the action→check→outcome→reaction cycle across modes.
  • Scene & Encounter Structure: a stepwise procedure with checklists and examples.
  • Mechanics Overview (GM): DCs, tiers, tags/conditions, clocks—your core levers.
  • Combat (GM Guidance): order options, action types, terrain/tags, clocks, resolve.
  • Designing & Running Enemies/Threats: roles, ranks, budgets, counterplay, behaviors.
  • Worked Examples & Case Studies: annotated walkthroughs across modes.
  • Advanced GM Guidance: improvisation, mysteries/politics, tone, table safety.
  • Worldbuilding & Prep Tools: usable templates and time‑saving workflows.

Cross‑Links

  • Player Guide: core concepts for players
  • Mechanics Reference: skills, proficiencies, tags, conditions
  • Storyteller Guide: narrative structure and campaign planning

Overview

Purpose: set expectations and give GMs immediate confidence. The GM’s mission is to keep play moving, make stakes visible, apply rules consistently, and turn every result into story momentum. This guide is practical first: short procedures, worked examples, and clear tools you can reach for in the moment. You’ll find pacing techniques that prevent stalls, adjudication patterns that keep rulings fair, and structure that translates rolls into fiction without losing vibe or speed. Whether you’re a first‑time GM or a veteran learning this system, these chapters show how to frame scenes, pick the right checks, use tags and conditions as levers, and bring pressure or relief through clocks. The core promise: you always know what happens next and why it feels right. — title: “Gameplay Philosophy” slug: gm-gameplay-philosophy doc_type: book version: 0.1.0 last_updated: 2025-11-08 keywords: [ttrpg, gm, philosophy] —

Gameplay Philosophy

Table of Contents

  • Why Principles Matter
  • The Principles
  • Applying Principles
  • Common Pitfalls
  • Cross‑Links

Why Principles Matter

Principles help you adjudicate quickly and fairly. They keep play moving, prevent stalls, and make outcomes feel earned. Use them as tiebreakers when the rules have multiple valid readings, and as prompts when the table hesitates. Stated out loud, they calibrate expectations so players know what success and costs look like before dice hit the table.

The Principles

  • Make Stakes Visible: Say what Full/Partial/Fail mean before rolling. Players commit more boldly when they can see outcomes.
  • Fail Forward: On a failure, change the situation (time, position, attention, resources) instead of stopping the story. New problems beat dead ends.
  • Fiction First, Numbers Follow: Let tags, conditions, and position drive DCs and advantage—not the other way around.
  • Progress and Pressure: Use paired clocks so effort makes headway even under threat. Partial success often ticks pressure you pre‑stated.
  • Spotlight is a Resource: Order and pacing should give everyone meaningful moments. Invite action and rotate cleanly.
  • State Changes, Not Gotchas: When mechanics bite, show the lever to clear or mitigate (aid, retreat, first aid, time). Pain is interesting when it creates choices.

Applying Principles

Exploration (Fog and Time): Pre‑state “Full crosses 2; Partial crosses 1 and ticks Patrol 1; Fail ticks Patrol 2.” Tags like Dim can grant advantage to stealth while raising DCs for navigation. On Partial, you still move forward.

Social (Leverage and Cost): Pre‑state “Full: clean approval; Partial: approval with strings; Fail: scrutiny rises.” If the room is Crowded, increase DCs until someone creates space (Set Up). Costs change future checks, not player agency.

Combat (Space and Pressure): Pre‑state beats for Set Up/Strike/Maneuver. Partial fills Reinforcements you telegraphed; Full degrades cover or advances the objective. Make the lever to reset (Withdraw, Clear) obvious.

Downtime (Projects and Heat): Every pass advances a project clock. On Partial, advance a complication you named beforehand (Heat 1). Provide ways to reduce complications if players choose to address them.

Common Pitfalls

  • Hidden DCs and Surprise Costs: If players can’t predict outcomes, they can’t make informed choices. Pre‑state stakes and why DCs look the way they do.
  • Binary Gates: Avoid “try again later” without change. Ask what would change the situation—then play that change.
  • Pacing Drift: Long turns and empty narration drain tension. Keep loop passes tight and close on change.

Core Rules for the GM

Table of Contents

  • When to Roll
  • Calling for Checks
  • DC Ladder & Outcome Tiers
  • Advantage/Disadvantage from Fiction
  • Group Checks & Contests
  • Turning Results into State
  • Cross‑Links

When to Roll

Roll only when both are true:

  • Uncertainty exists (the outcome could plausibly go multiple ways)
  • Stakes are present (something changes on Full/Partial/Fail)

Do not roll when a competent character succeeds with time and no pressure in the way (call it a success and move on). If failure would stall the game, add a cost and let play continue (fail‑forward).

Calling for Checks

Clarify three things out loud before dice:

  • Intent: what the player wants to accomplish
  • Approach: how they do it (which suggests tools/skills)
  • Tool: the skill/proficiency or contest involved

Then pick a DC from the fiction (see ladder below) and pre‑state what Full/Partial/Fail mean here. If needed, ask a question to expose leverage: “What are you risking?” or “How do you create an opening first?”

DC Ladder & Outcome Tiers

DC cues (choose what the fiction suggests)

  • 12 Easy: safe, aided, trivial with time
  • 14 Routine: standard challenge, normal tools
  • 16 Tough: notable risk, bad angle, poor tools
  • 18 Hard: steep odds, strong opposition, tight window
  • 20 Heroic: exceptional, stacked against, slim margin
  • 22 Legendary: near impossible without setup or luck

Tiers (translate into fiction)

  • Full: objective achieved cleanly; tick progress or gain position
  • Partial: progress with cost; fill pre‑stated pressure or apply a tag
  • Fail: no progress; escalate danger; reveal a new obstacle or cost
  • Crits: amplify change; consider clearing a small tag on crit success

Advantage/Disadvantage from Fiction

Position first, then numbers. Grant Advantage when approach, tools, or setup meaningfully help (elevated angle, quiet space, expert tools, ally assist). Impose Disadvantage when space, time, or attention meaningfully hinder (cramped footing, loud crowd, bad light, rushed timing). Create advantage by Set Up or helping; reduce disadvantage by changing space or timing.

Group Checks & Contests

Group checks

  • Majority: succeed if most do; Partial if split
  • All‑Must‑Succeed: use when a single failure breaks the attempt
  • Leader‑with‑Help: leader rolls; up to +2 aid dice from helpers

Contests

  • Both sides roll; higher total wins; ties are Partial by default
  • Pre‑state what Full/Partial/Fail mean for each side

Turning Results into State

Always update visible state. Prefer state changes that the table can feel now:

  • Tags: environmental or situational changes (Dim, Fragile Cover, Exposed)
  • Conditions: character states with clear clears (Exhausted, Restrained)
  • Clocks: paired progress/pressure to pace scenes (sizes 4/6/8)

Patterns

  • On Full: tick progress; clear or reduce a minor tag on a crit
  • On Partial: tick pre‑stated pressure; add a tag or impose a minor condition
  • On Fail: no progress; escalate pressure; reveal a new obstacle

GM usage

  • Say what changed and point to it on the table
  • Offer a meaningful follow‑up choice that uses or flips the new state

Cross‑Links

  • Scene procedure and transitions: Scene & Encounter Structure

The Gameplay Loop

Table of Contents

  • Expansion Plan
  • What the Loop Is
  • The Core Cycle
  • Information Flow & Stakes
  • Loop Variants by Mode
  • Table Cadence & Spotlight
  • Worked Micro Examples
  • Cross‑Links

Expansion Plan

  • Define a single, repeatable sequence that covers exploration, social, combat, and downtime.
  • Provide tiered outcomes (Full/Partial/Fail) with DC ladder cues and visible state updates (tags, conditions, clocks).
  • Include four micro examples (one per mode) showing the loop in action.

What the Loop Is

The gameplay loop is the conversation engine of your table: players declare intent, you judge risk, dice resolve uncertainty, and the world changes in ways everyone can feel. The loop is fast, visible, and fair—never stalling on binary gates. Progress and pressure move through clocks, tags, and conditions so that success or cost always pushes the fiction forward.

GM Usage: Keep the loop explicit. Name what success looks like, what a Partial costs, and how a Failure escalates pressure.

The Core Cycle

Ask → Declare → Judge → Resolve → Update → Ask

  1. Ask: “What do you do?” Focus on the present situation and objective.
  2. Declare: Players state clear intent and approach; you clarify details.
  3. Judge: Choose tool (skill/proficiency), pick a DC from the ladder (12 easy · 14 routine · 16 tough · 18 hard · 20 heroic · 22 legendary), apply advantage/disadvantage from fiction.
  4. Resolve: Roll and interpret tiered outcomes (Full/Partial/Fail/Crit).
  5. Update: Tick progress/pressure clocks; add/remove tags; impose/clear conditions; reveal new information.
  6. Ask again: Offer a meaningful follow‑up choice to continue momentum.

Alignment note: This loop maps directly onto the Scene procedure (Frame → Stakes → Check → Narrate → React). Use the loop to pace conversation and the scene steps to structure decisions and outcomes.

Loop at the Table (Tip)

  • Keep it short: resolve a concrete objective or escalate pressure, then ask.
  • Name levers: say which tags/conditions/clocks are in play right now.
  • Pre‑state beats: say Full/Partial/Fail before dice; prefer motion over stalls.
  • Offer choices: every update should open at least two meaningful next actions.

Information Flow & Stakes

  • Pre‑state beats: say what Full/Partial/Fail mean before rolling.
  • Tick complication clocks on Partial only when you’ve pre‑stated them.
  • Make costs move the story: time, noise, position, resources, attention. Avoid dead ends.
  • Keep state visible: display clocks; call out tags/conditions when they change.
  • Tie fiction to numbers: DCs reflect situational leverage, not hidden math.

Loop Variants by Mode

Exploration: Emphasize mapping, concealment, time, and environmental tags. Progress and pressure clocks pace travel, stealth, and hazards.

Social: Emphasize leverage, credibility, and audience mood. Costs create obligations, scrutiny, and changed access rather than hard denials.

Combat: Emphasize order/spotlight and space control. Partial results often fill pressure clocks (reinforcements, structural collapse) or degrade cover/tags.

Downtime: Emphasize projects and recovery. Each loop pass advances a project clock; costs introduce complications, rivals, or time slips.

Table Cadence & Spotlight

  • Rotate cleanly: after each resolve/update, point to someone with an immediate hook.
  • Group when helpful: treat a team action as one loop pass with help/aid resolving internally.
  • Use popcorn ordering in tense scenes to keep urgency; anchor key beats (e.g., defenses) if needed.
  • Keep loops short: resolve a concrete objective or escalate pressure, then ask again.

Worked Micro Examples

Reminder: Only tick complication clocks on Partial when you have pre‑stated them for the scene or beat.

Exploration — “Lantern Bridge”

Setup: A rickety bridge spans a misty ravine at night. Objective: cross quietly before patrols circle back.

Tags: Dim, Slick, Swaying Planks. Clocks: Progress — Crossed (4); Pressure — Patrol Returns (6).

Checks: Balance/Acrobatics (DC 16, Tough) to move safely; Stealth (DC 14, Routine) to muffle clatter. Dim can grant Advantage to Stealth if moving slowly.

Outcomes:

  • Full: Tick Crossed 2. “You pace your steps; the boards barely whisper.”
  • Partial: Tick Crossed 1 and Patrol 1; add Tag: Loose Board. “One plank flexes and groans—time is slipping.”
  • Fail: No progress; Patrol +2; impose Condition: Shaken or Tag: Loud Footfalls. “A plank snaps; echoes carry into the fog.”

Follow‑up: Ask whether to press quickly (drop Advantage) or slow down (risk Patrol).

Social — “Closed Kitchen”

Setup: The head chef has closed the kitchen; the party needs access to prep an antidote.

Tags: Overworked Staff, Hot Line (Distracting). Clock: Pressure — Management Scrutiny (6).

Checks: Negotiation (DC 16, Tough) to secure an exception; Performance (DC 14, Routine) to rally staff; Streetwise (DC 14, Routine) to find a sympathetic sous‑chef.

Outcomes:

  • Full: Access granted; note an ally in the brigade.
  • Partial: Access with strings (tight window or a favor); tick Scrutiny 1.
  • Fail: Denied for now; Scrutiny +2; add Tag: Flagged Request.

Follow‑up: Offer a tradeoff—accept a shorter window (reduced margin) or do a quick task to clear Flagged Request.

Combat — “Warehouse Standoff”

Setup: Smugglers take cover among crates; the party wants to seize the ledger.

Tags: Solid Cover (Crates), Dim, Narrow Aisles. Clocks: Progress — Secure Ledger (4); Pressure — Reinforcements (6).

Typical Beats: Set Up (create angle), Strike (contest vs cover), Maneuver (flank or shove), Defend/Withdraw to reset.

Checks: Set Up (DC 14, Routine) to climb a gantry for angle; Strike contests vs defender; Maneuver (DC 16, Tough) to shove an enemy from cover.

Outcomes (example Strike):

  • Full: Tick Ledger 2; degrade enemy cover (Fragile → Spent).
  • Partial: Tick Ledger 1; Reinforcements +1; add Tag: Exposed Position.
  • Fail: No progress; Reinforcements +2; Condition: Suppressed.

Follow‑up: Offer choices—clear Suppressed by withdrawing (time cost) or gamble on a Set Up to flip Exposed.

Downtime — “Decode the Ledger”

Setup: After the standoff, the party decodes ciphered entries to expose the ring.

Project Clock: Expose Operation (6). Complication Clock: Heat (6).

Checks: Research/Cryptography (DC 16, Tough) for progress; Contacts/Streetwise (DC 14, Routine) to source context and reduce DCs by creating advantage.

Outcomes per pass:

  • Full: Tick Expose 2; note a lead.
  • Partial: Tick Expose 1 and Heat 1.
  • Fail: Heat +2; add Tag: Tipped Hand (future social checks start at DC +2 until cleared).

Follow‑up: Choose to pursue a side scene to clear Tipped Hand or press on and accept future friction.

Scene & Encounter Structure

Table of Contents

  • Expansion Plan
  • Framing Scenes
  • Stakes, Costs, and Outcomes
  • Pacing with Clocks
  • Ending & Transitioning
  • Worked Examples
  • Cross‑Links

Expansion Plan

  • Synthesize best practices from rules into a retail-grade, stepwise procedure (frame → set stakes → check → narrate → react).
  • Add two fully annotated examples (exploration and social) with DC cues and Partial beats.
  • Provide a one‑page checklist sidebar for live facilitation.

Framing Scenes

Framing Checklist

  • Where are we? (location + relevant tags)
  • Who is here? (PCs/NPCs, intent, leverage)
  • What matters? (objective, resources at risk)
  • Why now? (time pressure, clock states)
  • What could change? (stakes on Full/Partial/Fail)

GM Prompts: “What do you do?” “What would success look like?” “What are you risking?”

Procedure (Frame → Stakes → Check → Narrate → React)

  1. Frame: Paint only what matters now. Name 1–2 Tags on the space (e.g., Dim, Crowded, Slick) that will actually influence play.
  2. Stakes: Say what Full / Partial / Fail mean before dice. Tie at least one outcome to a clock or tag change.
  3. Check: Pick the right tool (Skill/Proficiency) and a DC from the ladder (12 easy · 14 routine · 16 tough · 18 hard · 20 heroic · 22 legendary). Consider Advantage/Disadvantage from fiction, not numbers alone.
  4. Narrate: Translate the tier result into fiction. On Partial, introduce pressure (tick a clock, impose a Tag/Condition) but let progress continue.
  5. React: Update clocks, tags, positions, and ask the table what they do next. Offer a meaningful follow‑up choice.

Sidebar — Clean Framing (Quicklist)

  • State objective and why it matters now
  • Name 1–2 tags that will actually influence play
  • Pre‑state Full/Partial/Fail and any pressure clocks in effect
  • Point to a clear follow‑up choice after the first outcome

Stakes, Costs, and Outcomes

Outcome Matrix

  • Critical Success: objective plus advantage (free clear, bonus position)
  • Full Success: objective achieved cleanly; tick progress if applicable
  • Partial Success: objective with cost or complication; tick pressure or apply tag/condition
  • Failure: no objective; escalate danger; reveal new obstacle or cost
  • Critical Failure: decisive turn against PCs; trigger a major pressure event

GM Usage: Pre‑state beats; prefer costs that move the story (time, position, resource, attention) over binary denial.

Tier Cues (quick examples)

  • Full: “You cross unseen and arrive on the balcony.” (Tick progress 1)
  • Partial: “You cross, but guards grow suspicious.” (Tick pressure 1: Suspicion; add Tag: Exposed)
  • Fail: “You’re spotted; a horn sounds.” (Advance Reinforcements 2; add Condition: Pinned)

Always frame costs the table can feel: time lost, noise made, cover broken, resources drained, attention drawn.

Pacing with Clocks

Clock Patterns

  • Progress vs Pressure: fill progress on Full; pressure on Partial/Fail
  • Sizes: 4/6/8 segments; pick based on scene length and risk
  • Chains: allow one clock to spill into another at thresholds
  • Visuals: keep clocks visible; fear rises as hands advance

Sizing advice

  • Short, punchy scenes: 4‑segment progress and 4‑segment pressure
  • Standard, tense scenes: 6‑segment progress and 6‑segment pressure
  • Extended set pieces: 8‑segment progress; 6‑segment pressure (pressure resolves faster)

Ending & Transitioning

Close on resolution (progress full) or consequence (pressure full). Summarize change: how the fiction looks different. Offer momentum hooks: “Do you press your advantage?” “Do you regroup?” Update tags/conditions; clear what makes sense; tick campaign clocks.

Worked Examples

  • Exploration: “Fogbound Orchard” (mystery/horror); uses Thick Fog, Survival; show Partial consequences.
  • Social: “Festival Permit” (cozy); uses Crowded, Negotiation; show mixed outcomes and costs.

Outline Details

  • Fogbound Orchard: stakes (find healer’s herb before night); tags (Thick Fog, Slick); DC ladder for Survey/Navigation; Partial fills Suspicion wildlife clock; Fail triggers misstep hazard.
  • Festival Permit: stakes (secure permit before parade); tag (Crowded); DCs for Negotiation and Event Planning; Partial wins permit with strings (task or schedule change); Fail draws bureaucratic scrutiny clock.

Worked Example 1 — Fogbound Orchard (Exploration)

Setup: The party must locate a rare herb before nightfall to save an injured villager. The orchard sits in a valley; fog rolls in at dusk.

Tags in play: Dim, Obscuring (Thick Fog); Slick (mud) Clocks: Progress — Herb Found (6). Pressure — Night & Predators (6).

Framing: “You stand at the orchard’s edge. Fog curls between low trees and clings to your boots. If you succeed, you’ll find the herb before night. On a Partial, you’ll find signs and lose time; on a Failure, you’ll veer off, drawing things that hunt by sound.”

Action: Survey the orchard and navigate quietly. Checks:

  • Perception/Survival (DC 16, Tough) to orient by growth patterns and wind.
  • Stealth (DC 14, Routine) to keep noise low; Dim grants Advantage if moving slowly.

Results:

  • Full: Tick Herb Found 2; describe a clear trail of dew‑heavy leaves leading inward.
  • Partial: Tick Herb Found 1 and Night & Predators 1; add Tag: Off‑Track. “You find crushed stems—close—but your path circles a low bog.”
  • Fail: No progress; tick Night & Predators 2; impose Condition: Winded or Tag: Loud Footfalls (player choice). “A branch snaps; the orchard answers with sudden silence.”

On Critical Success: Clear Off‑Track or remove Loud Footfalls, and tick Herb Found 2 as you discover a direct path through leaning trunks.

Follow‑ups: Offer choices—press deeper with speed (drop Advantage) or slow down (protect Advantage, risk time). On a later Crit, allow clearing Off‑Track or removing Loud Footfalls.

GM Usage: Keep both clocks visible. Narrate fog as a lever: better stealth, worse navigation. On Partial, pay with time or attention, not dead ends.

Worked Example 2 — Festival Permit (Social)

Setup: The party must secure an event permit before the parade starts. The office is jammed; the clerk is overworked and by‑the‑book.

Tag in play: Crowded (noise distracts, +2 DC to serious requests unless you control space) Clock: Pressure — Bureaucratic Scrutiny (6): inspections, missing forms, manager’s review.

Framing: “If you succeed, the permit is granted cleanly. On a Partial, you get it with strings—an errand or a delay. On a Failure, scrutiny rises—someone higher up notices you.”

Actions: Negotiation (Find Middle), Event Planning (Schedule), and Streetwise (Find Ally in Line). Checks:

  • Negotiation (DC 16, Tough): reasoned case; Crowded raises to DC 18 unless you create quiet space (Set Up).
  • Event Planning (DC 14, Routine): present a safe route with contingencies.
  • Streetwise (DC 14, Routine): enlist a regular to vouch; converts Crowded to Helpful once per scene.

Results:

  • Full: Permit granted; note an inspector ally. “Your plan anticipates their concerns; stamp, signature, done.”
  • Partial: Permit granted with condition: complete a quick community task or accept a narrower window; tick Scrutiny 1.
  • Fail: Permit delayed; Scrutiny +2; add Tag: Flagged Application. “The manager wants to ‘take a look’—soon.”

Follow‑ups: Offer tradeoffs—accept narrower scope (reduced footprint) for time saved, or take the task to clear Flagged Application. Use the ally to flip Crowded into a boon for one check.

GM Usage: Make noise and space tangible levers. Partial outcomes should create choices that keep the festival moving, not stonewall it.

Cross‑Links

  • Tags & Conditions: environmental levers
  • Skills & Proficiencies: which rolls appear in scenes

  • GM Combat: see ordering and hazards for fight scenes

Mechanics Overview (GM‑Facing)

Table of Contents

  • What You Must Know
  • The Dice System
  • DC Ladder & Outcome Tiers
  • Advantage/Disadvantage & Position
  • Tags & Conditions as Levers
  • Clocks & Resources
  • Group Checks & Contests
  • GM Usage Quicklist
  • Cross‑Links

What You Must Know

  • The loop: Ask → Declare → Judge → Resolve → Update → Ask.
  • Pick DCs from fiction: leverage, risk, tools, tags.
  • Pre‑state stakes: Full/Partial/Fail beats before rolling.
  • Always move forward: failures change state; they do not stall.
  • Keep state visible: clocks, tags, conditions on the table.

The Dice System

This game uses 4d6 (four six-sided dice) as its core resolution mechanic. Here’s what you need to know as GM:

Basic Roll: Player rolls 4d6, sums all dice, adds relevant bonus, compares to DC you set. The roll averages 14 (before bonuses), creating a bell curve where most results cluster near the middle while extremes remain rare.

Advantage/Disadvantage: These modify the dice pool, not the DC.

  • Advantage comes in two levels: +1 (roll 5d6, keep best 4) or +2 (roll 6d6, keep best 4)
  • Disadvantage comes in two levels: -1 (roll 5d6, keep worst 4) or -2 (roll 6d6, keep worst 4)
  • Multiple sources net out, capping at ±2 levels. If a character has both, they cancel (e.g., +1 advantage and -1 disadvantage = roll normally)

Outcome Tiers by Margin: Calculate Roll - DC to get the margin:

  • Critical Success: Margin ≥+5 (spectacularly exceeded)
  • Full Success: Margin ≥0 (cleanly achieved)
  • Partial Success: Margin -1 to -2 (achieved with cost)
  • Failure: Margin ≤-3 (goal not achieved, situation escalates)
  • Critical Failure: Margin ≤-7 OR all 1s rolled (disaster)

GM Usage: You never roll for the world—you set DCs and interpret results. When players roll, you translate margins into fiction. A margin of +8 isn’t “you rolled high”—it’s “you pick the lock silently, find a hidden compartment, and recognize the maker’s mark.”

Detailed rules: See Rolling Dice in Mechanics Reference for complete mechanics with examples.

DC Ladder & Outcome Tiers

DC cues (pick what the fiction suggests)

  • 12 Easy: safe, aided, trivial with time
  • 14 Routine: standard challenge, normal tools
  • 16 Tough: notable risk, bad angle, poor tools
  • 18 Hard: steep odds, strong opposition, tight window
  • 20 Heroic: exceptional, stacked against, slim margin
  • 22 Legendary: near impossible without setup or luck

Outcome tiers (translate into fiction)

  • Full: objective achieved cleanly; tick progress or gain position
  • Partial: progress with cost; fill pressure you pre‑stated or apply a tag
  • Fail: no progress; escalate danger; reveal a new obstacle or cost
  • Crits: amplify change; on crit success consider clearing a minor tag

Advantage/Disadvantage & Position

Grant Advantage when approach, tools, or setup meaningfully help. Impose Disadvantage when space, time, or attention meaningfully hinder. Position describes how safe and effective a move is; shift position first, then pick numbers. Create Advantage by setting up, controlling space, or getting help.

Micro cues

  • Advantage: elevated angle, quiet space, expert tools, ally assist
  • Disadvantage: cramped footing, loud crowd, bad light, rushed timing

Tags & Conditions as Levers

Tags describe the environment or temporary states (Dim, Slick, Cramped, Fragile Cover). Conditions change a character’s capabilities (Exhausted, Restrained, Bleeding). Apply them when outcomes change reality; show clear ways to clear or mitigate.

GM usage

  • Name 1–2 meaningful tags per scene; make effects explicit
  • On Partial, prefer adding a tag or ticking pressure over denial
  • Offer clears: first aid, time, leverage, change of approach

Clocks & Resources

Use paired clocks to pace progress and pressure. Pick sizes from tempo (4/6/8). Fill progress on Full; tick pressure on Partial/Fail as pre‑stated. Resources (gear, spell slots, favors) are levers: spend to change position or DCs.

Patterns

  • Short scenes: 4 progress, 4 pressure
  • Standard scenes: 6 progress, 6 pressure
  • Set pieces: 8 progress, 6 pressure (pressure resolves faster)

Group Checks & Contests

Group checks

  • Majority: succeed if most do; Partial if split
  • All‑Must‑Succeed: use when a single failure breaks the attempt
  • Leader‑with‑Help: leader rolls; up to +2 aid dice from helpers

Contests

  • Both sides roll; higher total wins; ties are Partial by default
  • Pre‑state what Full/Partial/Fail mean for each side

GM Usage Quicklist

  • Say stakes before dice; pick DC from fiction
  • Map tier to fiction; update tags, conditions, clocks
  • Prefer costs that move the story; offer clears
  • Rotate spotlight; keep passes short; ask again

Cross‑Links

  • Scene procedure and transitions: Scene & Encounter Structure
  • The core cycle: The Gameplay Loop
  • Combat ordering and hazards: Combat (GM Guidance)
  • Tags & Conditions (reference concepts): Tags and Conditions
  • Proficiencies overview (reference): Proficiencies — title: “Facilitating Character Creation” slug: gm-facilitating-character-creation doc_type: book version: 0.1.0 last_updated: 2025-11-08 keywords: [ttrpg, gm, session zero, character creation] —

Facilitating Character Creation

Table of Contents

  • Session Zero Agenda
  • Party Composition
  • Character Build Flow
  • Linking PCs
  • First Adventure Hooks
  • Cross‑Links

Session Zero Agenda

  • Safety check‑in: lines/veils, tone, red card protocol
  • Theme & tone: supported playstyles; examples of scenes we want/avoid
  • Table cadence: spotlight rotation, rulings (stakes before dice), visible state
  • Advancement expectations: pace and what “getting stronger” looks like here
  • Scheduling and logistics: session length, recap rhythm, notes

Party Composition

Coverage and spotlight

  • Roles and coverage: can the party pursue plans without a single gate?
  • Spotlight rules: rotate; invite quieter players first after resets
  • Safety valve: define how the party retreats or trades time for safety

GM usage

  • Ask for a party statement: “What do you do well together?”
  • If a gap is risky (e.g., no social leverage), plan an early hook to cover it

Character Build Flow

Walk players through choices; confirm what you need to adjudicate fairly.

Checklist

  • Concept → Role at the table
  • Skills/Proficiencies: what they’re best at; what’s weak
  • Tags/Conditions they bring or resist (e.g., Night‑Sight, Cloistered)
  • Gear/resources that change position (climbing kit, smoke, rally horn)
  • Flag: a personal hook the GM may pull (owed favor, rival, goal)

Linking PCs

Create two links per PC: one practical, one personal.

Prompts

  • You owe them: debt, teaching, shared loss
  • You trust them for: a skill, a secret, a promise
  • You fear for them because: a weakness or enemy

GM usage

  • Turn links into immediate advantages (advantage on aid) or costs (Heat +1)

First Adventure Hooks

Pick 3–5 hooks and tailor to the chosen tone.

  • The Festival Permit: save the parade (Social/Logistics)
  • The Sunken Cloister: retrieve the reliquary before tide (Exploration)
  • Warehouse Ledger: seize and decode a smuggling ledger (Combat/Downtime)
  • Bridge Gate Push: force the gate to protect evacuees (Set Piece)
  • Threading the Heist: invite → infiltrate → extract (Multi‑Scene)

Cross‑Links

  • The core cycle: The Gameplay Loop
  • Scene procedure and transitions: Scene & Encounter Structure
  • Mechanics overview (GM cues): Mechanics Overview
  • Tags & Conditions (reference concepts): Tags and Conditions — title: “NPC Creation & Management” slug: gm-npc-creation doc_type: book version: 0.1.0 last_updated: 2025-11-08 keywords: [ttrpg, gm, npc] —

NPC Creation & Management

Table of Contents

  • NPC Roles & Goals
  • Fast NPC Template
  • Running NPCs
  • Maintenance
  • Cross‑Links

NPC Roles & Goals

  • Ally: provides aid, asks for help, changes with favors
  • Patron: resources and pressure; sets objectives
  • Foil: competes for the same goals; raises stakes without direct violence
  • Antagonist: actively opposes; pressures clocks; punishes stalling

Fast NPC Template

  • Name, Role, Goal, Leverage
  • Hooks (easy/risky):
    • Easy: the favor they’ll do if it costs little
    • Risky: the favor they’ll do if you pay a price
  • Weakness: what flips them (greed, pride, duty)
  • Tag/Condition: a lever they bring (Guarded, Overworked)
  • GM Usage: how they move scenes forward

Example: Clerk Sessa (Patron‑adjacent)

  • Hooks: Easy — stamp routine papers off‑hours; Risky — expedite a late permit
  • Weakness: pride in being fair; don’t insult their duty
  • Tag: Overworked (Crowded raises DCs unless space is controlled)

Running NPCs

  • State what they want right now; update when facts change
  • Use Hooks to turn talk into action; offer price for risky favors
  • On Partial, change what they watch or demand (Scrutiny +1; Flagged Request)

Maintenance

  • Session log: note goal shifts, new leverage, and changed tags
  • Flags: record player promises and debts
  • Evolution: promote/demote roles as the campaign shifts

Cross‑Links

  • Scene procedure and transitions: Scene & Encounter Structure
  • The core cycle: The Gameplay Loop
  • NPC catalog (reference): NPCs
  • Tags & Conditions (reference concepts): Tags and Conditions — title: “VPC Creation & Management” slug: gm-vpc-creation doc_type: book version: 0.1.0 last_updated: 2025-11-08 keywords: [ttrpg, gm, vpc, villain] —

VPC Creation & Management

Table of Contents

  • VPC Roles & Knobs
  • VPC Template
  • Running VPCs
  • Cross‑Links

VPC Roles & Knobs

  • Mastermind (Controller/Leader): plans, delegates, escapes
  • Brute (Defender/Skirmisher): pressure in space; breaks lines
  • Sorcerer/Engineer (Artillery/Controller): area denial; tools and rituals

Knobs (what you can turn)

  • Resources: lieutenants, gear, favors
  • Space: lair tags and hazards; safe rooms, kill zones
  • Attention: how widely they are known; Heat they draw

VPC Template

  • Role, Goal, Public Face, True Drive
  • Knobs (list 3): what changes if each is turned
  • Behavior Script (Opening, Mid, Exit)
  • Counterplay: how PCs flip the script
  • Exit Strategy: when they retreat, concede, or pivot

Example: The Bookkeeper (Mastermind)

  • Knobs: double‑entry ledgers (resource); bribeable inspectors (attention); safe room under the counting house (space)
  • Script: Opening — cut communications; Mid — isolate and bribe; Exit — vanish through a ledger‑lined false wall
  • Counterplay: flip an inspector, expose the safe room via Set Up, cut funds
  • Exit Strategy: concedes when exposed in public or Heat ≥4

Running VPCs

  • Pace reveals: turn one knob at a time; show what changed
  • Guard exits: the Exit Strategy is real; capture/confrontation is rare unless players deny the exit in fiction
  • On Partial, tick pre‑stated complications (Heat, Scrutiny) and show the VPC’s next lever

Cross‑Links

  • Designing threats and terrain: Designing & Running Enemies
  • Combat ordering and hazards: Combat (GM Guidance)
  • Worked patterns: Worked Examples
  • NPC catalog (reference): NPCs
  • VPC catalog (reference): VPCs
  • Tags & Conditions (reference concepts): Tags and Conditions — title: “Designing & Running Enemies/Threats” slug: gm-designing-running-enemies doc_type: book version: 0.1.0 last_updated: 2025-11-08 keywords: [ttrpg, gm, enemies, threats] —

Designing & Running Enemies/Threats

Table of Contents

  • Roles & Threat Ranks
  • Building Enemies
  • Encounter Budgets & Composition
  • Terrain & Synergy
  • Behavior Scripts
  • Worked Composition Example
  • Cross‑Links

Roles & Threat Ranks

Common roles

  • Skirmisher: mobile pressure; punishes isolation
  • Artillery: ranged damage/control; vulnerable in close
  • Controller: space denial; creates hazards and splits teams
  • Defender: anchors space; protects allies; punishes overreach
  • Leader: amplifies others; coordinates focus and retreats

Threat ranks (guidance)

  • T1 (Minor): a single misstep can drop them; 1 budget point
  • T2 (Standard): credible foe; survives a couple strong hits; 2 points
  • T3 (Elite): centerpiece of a scene; requires setup/flanks; 4 points
  • T4 (Champion): set piece; demands terrain and support; 6 points
  • T5 (Mythic): arc‑ender; treat as a scenario with phases; 10 points

Building Enemies

Start from the fiction. Give each enemy 2–3 levers the GM can actually use.

Pick

  • Attributes/Tags that matter (Slick Carapace, Bulky, Elevated Nest)
  • One signature move (Hook Net, Suppressing Fire, Shatter Roar)
  • One counterplay hook (break line of sight; bait a charge; disrupt chant)

GM usage

  • State what Full/Partial/Fail mean when players target the enemy’s lever
  • Telegraph counterplay via description and reactions
  • On Partial, change space or clocks; avoid binary denial

Encounter Budgets & Composition

Simple rubric (party of 4, adjust ±1 point per PC)

  • Low (4–5 points): skirmish; quick scene
  • Standard (6–8 points): main beat; 1–2 clocks in play
  • Hard (9–12 points): set piece; expect repositioning and retreats

Example (party of 5): add +1 point to the budget range — Low (5–6), Standard (7–9), Hard (10–13). For a party of 3, subtract 1 point: Low (3–4), Standard (5–7), Hard (8–11).

Composition patterns

  • One T3 + two T1s (elite with screens)
  • Two T2s + two T1s (paired threats with support)
  • One T2 + terrain hazard (controller + lever)

DC cues (pick from fiction)

  • 14 Routine: clear a screen, secure cover, suppress briefly
  • 16 Tough: break formation, disarm, shove through hazard
  • 18 Hard: disable a signature move under pressure

Terrain & Synergy

Terrain is a force multiplier. Name 1–2 tags that meaningfully change play, and make their effects explicit.

Examples

  • Cramped + Slick: favors defenders and controllers; shoves are risky
  • Elevated + Obscuring: favors artillery; demand Set Up to close safely
  • Fragile Cover + Reinforcement Clock: encourages maneuver to degrade cover

GM usage

  • On Partial, degrade cover, split teams, or tick pressure clocks you named
  • Offer lines of play that flip the lever (clear cover, create quiet, flood the light)

Behavior Scripts

Scripts keep spotlight moving and enemy choices legible.

Template

  • Opening: establish role/lever (Skirmisher flanks; Controller seeds hazard)
  • Mid‑fight: press advantage; protect lever; call for help on pressure 3+
  • Exit: retreat when objective met or resolve low; offer parley/surrender

Worked Composition Example

“Bridge Gate Push” (standard, 8 points; party of 4)

Tags: Cramped, Slick, Chokepoint. Clocks: Progress — Gate Forced (6); Pressure — Reinforcements (6).

Foes (8 points)

  • T3 Troll Gatekeeper (Defender/Controller): Shove to River (contest vs Maneuver), Regenerate in rain; Counterplay: grease planks or blind the eye
  • Two T1 Spear Guards (Skirmishers): Pin Down at the chokepoint; Counterplay: pull them off line with bait
  • Terrain Hazard: Slick Planks (Tag): impose Disadvantage on rushes unless secured

Beats & DC cues

  • Set Up to sand/salt planks (DC 14, Routine) removes Slick for one pass
  • Maneuver to shove the Troll (DC 16, Tough) or make space for two to rush
  • Strike against Troll behind cover: Partial degrades cover; Full ticks Gate 2

Outcomes (example Maneuver vs Troll)

  • Full: Troll moved; tick Gate Forced 2; cover degraded
  • Partial: Troll resists; Reinforcements +1; add Tag: Exposed Position
  • Fail: No progress; Reinforcements +2; Condition: Winded

GM usage

  • Telegraphed counterplay: show the slick boards and the eye; reward setup
  • On Partial, fill pressure you named; keep progress visible
  • Offer exits: parley after Gate Forced 4, or retreat on Pressure 5+

Worked Composition Variant — Alley Crossfire (Urban)

Tags: Cramped Alley, Fragile Cover (Crates), Elevated Balcony. Clocks: Progress — Ringleader Cornered (6); Pressure — Patrol (6).

Foes (7 points, party of 4)

  • T2 Ringleader (Leader/Skirmisher): Calls shots; Counterplay: cut sightlines
  • Two T1 Lookouts (Artillery): Crossfire from balcony; Counterplay: smoke, Set Up
  • T1 Knife Runner (Skirmisher): Flanks; Counterplay: block lanes, trip

Beats & DC cues

  • Set Up (DC 14) smoke or tarp to break crossfire; degrades Fragile cover
  • Maneuver (DC 16) to reach the balcony; risk Exposed if you rush
  • Strike vs Lookout in cover: Partial degrades cover; Full ticks Ringleader 2

Outcomes (example Set Up)

  • Full: Crossfire broken; tick Ringleader Cornered 2
  • Partial: Crossfire reduced; Patrol +1
  • Fail: No progress; Patrol +2; Tag: Exposed Position

Cross‑Links

  • Combat ordering and hazards: Combat (GM Guidance)
  • Scene procedure and transitions: Scene & Encounter Structure
  • Tags & Conditions (reference concepts): Tags and Conditions
  • Enemy catalogs (reference): Enemies — title: “Combat (GM Guidance)” slug: gm-combat-guidance doc_type: book version: 0.1.0 last_updated: 2025-11-07 keywords: [ttrpg, gm, combat] —

Combat (GM Guidance)

Table of Contents

  • Expansion Plan
  • Order & Spotlight
  • Action Types & Adjudication
  • Terrain, Tags, and Conditions
  • Pacing with Clocks
  • Resolve without HP (Options)
  • Worked Examples
  • Cross‑Links

Expansion Plan

  • Integrate core mechanics into a GM‑facing procedure for fast, fair combat.
  • Add 2–3 worked beats (alley ambush, bridge fray, rooftop chase) with DC/tiers and tag usage.
  • Provide a micro‑checklist for live use (ordering, call stakes, apply tags, narrate beats).

Order & Spotlight

Ordering Modes

  • Conversational: ask “Who acts?”; rotate spotlight; break ties by danger/sense
  • Popcorn: current actor names next; alternate sides; prevents alpha strike
  • Hybrid: key beats have fixed order; between beats use conversational

Popcorn phrasing (example): “You’re up, then name who acts next.” Rotate across sides to spread momentum.

Group Checks: Majority / All‑Must‑Succeed / Leader‑with‑Help (advantage dice up to +2). Contests: both roll; higher total wins; ties are Partial by default.

Action Types & Adjudication

Core Actions

  • Strike: contest vs defender or passive DC (14 + defense bonus)
  • Maneuver: shove, trip, disarm, reposition; on Partial trade space/position for safety
  • Set Up: create advantage or reduce DC; often applies tags/cover
  • Defend/Withdraw: change position/effect; clear a minor tag; break contact

Adjudication: Pre‑state tier beats; use DC ladder (12/14/16/18/20/22); fiction may grant Advantage/Disadvantage.

Micro Example — Withdraw Clears Suppressed

You are Suppressed behind Fragile cover. On your turn, choose Withdraw: fall back to sturdier crates (change position), clear Suppressed, and give up the shot this pass. Next pass, a Set Up from an ally can restore a safe angle.

Terrain, Tags, and Conditions

Cover as Tag: Fragile vs Solid; Partial often degrades Fragile. Elevation, Dim/Obscuring, Slick/Cramped: name the lever; explain its effect on DC/Advantage. Conditions (Bleeding, Exhausted, Restrained) impose clear state changes with obvious clears (first aid, time, leverage).

Pacing with Clocks

Progress (wear down a notable foe or secure objective) vs Pressure (reinforcements, collapse, fire spread). On Partial, prefer filling Pressure; on Crit, consider ticking both. Use 4/6/8 segments based on tempo.

GM cue: On Partial, prefer ticking a pre‑stated pressure clock or degrading Fragile cover rather than denying progress outright.

Resolve without HP (Options)

Resolve Clocks (by threat): T1:2–3, T2:4, T3:6, T4:8, T5:10 — filling breaks will/position/gear. Morale & Breaks: end fights when objectives met or opposition collapses. End early if the fiction makes continued rolling redundant.

Worked Examples

  • Alley Ambush (modern)
  • Bridge Fray (fantasy)
  • Rooftop Pursuit (mystery)

Outline Details

  • Alley Ambush: tags (Dim, Crowded); foes (T2 skirmisher + T1 thugs); examples of Set Up/Strike/Maneuver; Partial ticks Reinforcements; cover degrades.
  • Bridge Fray: tags (Cramped, Slick); Troll (resolve clock 4); show Shove risk and group check to rush the gate.
  • Rooftop Pursuit: tags (Elevated, Obscuring); contests for leaps, leader‑with‑help coordination; Partial splits team briefly; Fail triggers stumble clock.

Cross‑Links

  • Combat Quick Reference (core)
  • Enemies/Threats chapter (GM)

  • Tags & Conditions (mechanics)

Worked Examples & Case Studies

Table of Contents

  • Exploration — The Sunken Cloister
  • Social — The Minister’s Audience
  • Combat — Rail Yard Skirmish
  • Downtime — Workshop Season
  • Multi‑Scene — Threading the Heist
  • Cross‑Links

Exploration — The Sunken Cloister

Setup: A flooded cloister lies beneath a ruined chapel. The party seeks a sealed reliquary before the night tide seals the passages.

Tags: Dim, Waist‑Deep Water, Slick Stone. Clocks: Progress — Reliquary Found (6); Pressure — Tide & Vermin (6).

Framing: “Full: you chart a safe path and reach the reliquary quickly. Partial: you advance, but time and noise draw vermin. Fail: you lose time or footing, and the cloister fights back.” GM Callout: name the water and stone as levers that shift Advantage/Disadvantage between stealth and movement.

Checks (examples)

  • Survey/Navigation (DC 16, Tough): read stonework and currents
  • Stealth (DC 14, Routine): keep kit from clanking and splashing
  • Athletics (DC 16, Tough): lift a fallen beam in the passage

Outcomes (Survey/Navigation)

  • Full: Tick Reliquary 2; note a pattern of carved fish pointing the way
  • Partial: Tick Reliquary 1 and Tide & Vermin 1; add Tag: Off‑Route
  • Fail: No progress; Tide & Vermin +2; Condition: Soaked or Strap Snapped

GM Usage: Dim can grant Advantage to stealth at the cost of speed; Off‑Route offers a later clear on a critical success. On Partial, tick the pre‑stated pressure; avoid dead ends. Follow‑up: “Press quickly with noise, or slow your breathing and lose time?”

Social — The Minister’s Audience

Setup: The party needs an emergency export waiver from the Trade Minister. The antechamber is crowded; aides guard the schedule.

Tags: Crowded, Formal Protocol. Clock: Pressure — Scrutiny (6).

Framing: “Full: you earn a same‑day waiver. Partial: you get a waiver with strings (narrowed scope or a favor). Fail: your request is flagged and stalled.” GM Callout: invite setup actions to reduce noise or gain a vouching ally before the main ask.

Checks (examples)

  • Negotiation (DC 16, Tough): case for urgency and fairness
  • Streetwise (DC 14, Routine): locate a friendly aide who can vouch
  • Event Planning (DC 14, Routine): present a route and safety contingencies

Outcomes (Negotiation)

  • Full: Waiver granted; note an aide contact for future pulls
  • Partial: Waiver granted with strings; Scrutiny +1
  • Fail: Waiver delayed; Scrutiny +2; Tag: Flagged Request

GM Usage: Crowded raises DCs for serious asks unless space is controlled or a vouch is secured. Offer clear tradeoffs: accept a narrower window for speed, or do a small favor to clear Flagged Request. Follow‑up: “Secure a quiet alcove or work the line for a vouch?”

Combat — Rail Yard Skirmish

Setup: Smugglers scatter among freight and ladders at a midnight rail yard. The party wants to seize a shipment ledger before reinforcements arrive.

Tags: Solid Cover (Freight), Elevated, Dim. Clocks: Progress — Ledger Secured (4); Pressure — Reinforcements (6).

Ordering: Use popcorn to keep tension high; declare who follows after each action. Invite Set Up to create angles and degrade cover.

Checks (examples)

  • Set Up (DC 14, Routine): climb a ladder for an angle or swing a lamp for light
  • Maneuver (DC 16, Tough): shove or flank to break a screen
  • Strike (contest): attack from angle vs cover and defender

Outcomes (Strike from angle)

  • Full: Tick Ledger 2; Fragile cover degrades to Spent
  • Partial: Tick Ledger 1; Reinforcements +1; Tag: Exposed Position
  • Fail: No progress; Reinforcements +2; Condition: Suppressed

GM Usage: Telegraph how to flip levers (light, height, cover). On Partial, prefer pressure or state changes over denial. Follow‑up: “Withdraw to clear Suppressed, or press with a Set Up to flip Exposed?”

Downtime — Workshop Season

Setup: Between missions, the party works to restore a storm‑damaged workshop. They also gather intel on the ledgers.

Project Clock: Workshop Restored (6). Complication Clock: Heat (6).

Checks (per pass)

  • Craft/Repair (DC 16, Tough): progress on the restoration
  • Research (DC 14, Routine): decode a symbol and reduce future DCs via notes
  • Contacts (DC 14, Routine): find a discreet buyer for the seized ledgers

Outcomes per pass

  • Full: Tick Workshop 2; note a useful tool or safety improvement
  • Partial: Tick Workshop 1 and Heat 1 (pre‑stated complication)
  • Fail: Heat +2; Tag: Tipped Hand (social checks +2 DC until cleared)

GM Usage: Offer options to clear complications: a side scene to reduce Heat or to spend favors on repairs. Follow‑up: “Press the build this week, or take a meeting to cool Heat?”

Multi‑Scene — Threading the Heist

Setup: A three‑beat heist: acquire an invite, infiltrate during a gala, and extract with the ledger intact. Show clean transitions and visible state.

Beat 1 — Acquire the Invite (Social)

Tags: Crowded, Music. Clock: Scrutiny (6).

Checks: Performance (DC 14) to impress; Negotiation (DC 16) for the ask; Streetwise (DC 14) to find a sympathetic usher.

Outcomes (Negotiation)

  • Full: Clean invite; usher friend noted
  • Partial: Invite with strings (time‑boxed or access limited); Scrutiny +1
  • Fail: No invite now; Scrutiny +2; Tag: Flagged

Transition: The invite’s limit sets a time window for infiltration; show Scrutiny on the table.

Beat 2 — Infiltration (Exploration/Stealth)

Tags: Dim, Crowded Corridors. Clocks: Progress — Vault Reached (6); Pressure — Attention (6).

Checks: Stealth (DC 14) to move through the crowd; Survey (DC 16) to map a short path; Set Up (DC 14) to create a diversion.

Outcomes (Stealth)

  • Full: Tick Vault 2; pass unnoticed
  • Partial: Tick Vault 1 and Attention 1; Tag: Exposed Position
  • Fail: No progress; Attention +2; Condition: Winded

Transition: At vault, resolve access using setup from Beat 1; Exposed Position lingers unless cleared.

Beat 3 — Extraction (Combat/Pursuit)

Tags: Elevated Walkway, Fragile Cover. Clocks: Progress — Extraction (4); Pressure — Reinforcements (6).

Note: If Exposed Position remains from prior beats, apply its effect to the first contest until cleared by fiction.

Checks: Maneuver (DC 16) to leap between cars; Strike (contest) to break a screen; Defend/Withdraw to reset.

Outcomes (Maneuver)

  • Full: Tick Extraction 2; gain cover
  • Partial: Tick Extraction 1; Reinforcements +1; Tag: Off‑Balance
  • Fail: No progress; Reinforcements +2; Condition: Shaken

GM Usage: Keep clocks visible across beats; let prior tags/conditions carry forward unless cleared by fiction. Offer an exit at Extraction 3+: “Slip away now or push for the full clear?”

Cross‑Links

  • The core cycle: The Gameplay Loop

  • Combat ordering and hazards: Combat (GM Guidance)

Advanced GM Guidance

Table of Contents

  • Improvisation Techniques
  • Running Intrigue & Mystery
  • Advanced Pacing & Spotlight
  • Safety & Tone Management
  • Troubleshooting
  • Cross‑Links

Improvisation Techniques

Build from player intent; treat your prep as levers, not scripts.

Patterns

  • Yes‑And with Costs: accept the idea; add a cost or complication
  • Reframe: reduce a stuck plan to a smaller objective and ask again
  • Reveal a Lever: show a tag/condition/clock that can change the situation
  • Fronts: list 3 forces with goals/timers; ask which advances now

GM usage

  • Name what success looks like; pre‑state Partial/Fail; then play to find out
  • Keep a page of names/roles/tags to slot quickly when you need an NPC/scene

Running Intrigue & Mystery

Information is a resource, not a wall. Let clues point to more than one place; let clocks and suspicion track risk, not “fail or stop.”

Tools

  • Clue Triangle: each scene points to two other leads; progress even on Partials
  • Suspicion Clocks: pre‑state what fills them; show what scrutiny changes
  • Heat & Attention: carry between scenes; offer ways to reduce

GM usage

  • On Full: give clarity and a new lead; tick progress
  • On Partial: give a messy lead and tick Suspicion/Heat 1
  • On Fail: escalate attention; reveal a complication or rival force

Advanced Pacing & Spotlight

  • Beats & Montages: compress unimportant steps; expand key choices
  • Nested Clocks: a set piece can have a progress clock and multiple pressures
  • Popcorn + Anchors: choose who acts next; anchor key beats (defenses/escapes)
  • Spotlight Rescue: if someone is quiet, point to a lever they can use now

GM usage

  • Close on a change in state; summarize and ask again
  • Alternate pressure across the party; avoid piling everything on one PC

Safety & Tone Management

Calibrate at session zero, then maintain in play.

Checklist

  • Lines/Veils reminders; check tone if a beat feels off
  • Recap without graphic detail; consent before revisiting sensitive content
  • Use safety tools (pause/rewind) without penalty to players

Troubleshooting

Common stalls and fixes

  • Analysis Paralysis: reframe to two options; put a gentle timer on the scene
  • Runaway Plan: call out pressure and risk; ask what they’re willing to pay
  • Missed Hook: reintroduce via a different lever (new NPC, tag, or clock)

Cross‑Links

  • The core cycle: The Gameplay Loop
  • Scene procedure and transitions: Scene & Encounter Structure
  • Mechanics overview (GM cues): Mechanics Overview
  • Worked patterns: Worked Examples
  • Combat ordering and hazards: Combat (GM Guidance)
  • Tags & Conditions (reference concepts): Tags and Conditions — title: “Storytelling Fundamentals” slug: gm-storytelling-fundamentals doc_type: book version: 0.1.0 last_updated: 2025-11-08 keywords: [ttrpg, gm, storytelling, beats, arcs] —

Storytelling Fundamentals

Table of Contents

  • Theme & Stakes
  • Beats & Arcs
  • Setup → Payoff
  • Pacing Tools
  • Tone & Genre Signals
  • Cross‑Links

Theme & Stakes

Theme says what the story is about. Stakes say why it matters now. Pick a theme for the current arc (e.g., debt, trust, identity) and name stakes each scene so players know what a result will change.

GM usage

  • Open scenes by stating immediate stakes
  • Tie scene outcomes back to the arc theme in recaps

Beats & Arcs

Think in layers of scale and compress/expand to fit your session.

Beats of a scene

  • Frame → Stakes → Check → Narrate → React (see Scene Structure)
  • Each pass should change state or escalate pressure

Arcs

  • Sequence (2–3 scenes) → Arc (3–6 sessions) → Campaign (multiple arcs)
  • Track arc‑level clocks (progress and pressure) alongside scene clocks

GM usage

  • At the end of a session, note which arc clocks changed
  • If an arc stalls, introduce a reveal or new lever that touches the theme

Setup → Payoff {#setup-→-payoff}

Plant details you can pay off later; reveal when players pull on them.

Tools

  • Foreshadow: hint at dangers or opportunities; show signs before effects
  • Callback: reprise an earlier element in a new context
  • Revelation: turn unknowns into choices with cost and benefit

GM usage

  • When you plant, write a sticky: what it suggests and how to pay it off
  • Pay off via a meaningful check and visible state change

Pacing Tools

Shape tension. Give space to breathe between hard choices.

Patterns

  • Tension Curve: alternate pressure with small relief; escalate per scene
  • Montage: compress routine steps; highlight one meaningful choice
  • Nested Clocks: run a set piece with a progress clock and 1–2 pressures

GM usage

  • Cut early when a choice is made; resume on the next lever
  • After a hard beat, offer a brief relief scene to reset spotlight and tone

Tone & Genre Signals

Tone comes from what you emphasize. Use mechanics to reinforce genre.

Signals

  • Cozy: softer costs; partials lean toward obligations/favors over harm
  • Mystery: reveal clues on Partials; advance suspicion/attention on Fails
  • Action: emphasize space/tags and pressure clocks; celebrate bold setup

GM usage

  • Say the tone at session zero; keep a short list of genre levers handy
  • When tone drifts, restate stakes in genre language and adjust costs

Cross‑Links

  • The core cycle: The Gameplay Loop
  • Scene procedure and transitions: Scene & Encounter Structure
  • Mechanics overview (GM cues): Mechanics Overview

  • Worked patterns and foreshadowing/payoff examples: Worked Examples

Worldbuilding Toolkit

Table of Contents

  • Principles
  • Region Template
  • Location Template
  • Faction Template
  • Culture Template
  • Hooks Generator
  • Cross‑Links

Principles

Playable first: build levers the table can use now. Prefer tags, clocks, and hooks over lore. Show how to flip a lever; state costs for doing so.

GM usage

  • Tag spaces with 1–2 meaningful properties; show clears/changes
  • Add fronts via clocks to pace regional threats
  • Write hooks as immediate choices, not backstory

Region Template

  • Name, Theme, One‑Sentence Pitch
  • Travel Tags (2–3): e.g., Cramped Passes, Sudden Fog, Treacherous Roads
  • Resources & Scarcities: what is abundant; what you must barter for
  • Fronts (2–3): each with a clock (6/8) and a visible signal
  • Factions Present: names, goals, leverage
  • Landmarks: 3 places that matter (with a tag and a secret each)

Example — The Mistwell March

  • Travel Tags: Sudden Fog, Slick Marsh Paths
  • Fronts: Smuggling Ring (Heat); Sinking Keystones (Collapse)
  • Landmarks: Toll Bridge (Fragile Cover; ledger hidden), Old Cloister (Dim; reliquary below), Orchard Edge (Obscuring; predators at dusk)

Location Template

  • Name, Purpose, Vibe
  • Tags (2–3): what changes checks and tactics here
  • Encounters (2): what scenes happen here (goal, pressure)
  • Secrets (2): a payoff for setup or a risk to reveal
  • Hooks (2–3): immediate reasons to visit now

GM usage

  • Write how a tag flips: e.g., “Quiet alcove reduces Crowded DC by 2 once”
  • Tie each secret to a lever the PCs can pull to reveal/payoff

Faction Template

  • Name, Goal, Public Face, True Leverage
  • Assets (3): people/gear/territory; what they risk to win
  • Counterplay: how PCs undermine them (expose, split, bargain)
  • Clock: Influence (6/8) with visible steps
  • Hooks (2): what they want from PCs now (easy/risky)

Example — The Bookkeepers’ Circle

  • Goal: launder contraband funds into public works
  • Assets: loyal clerks; black‑ledger network; inspector favors
  • Counterplay: seize ledgers; flip an inspector; freeze favors
  • Influence: 0→6 (stingy rebates → civic projects)
  • Hooks: Easy — small donation; Risky — alter a ledger entry

Culture Template

  • Values (3): what matters most here
  • Signals: names, styles, greetings (2–3 examples)
  • Tensions: internal pressures; what changes if one resolves
  • Customs: one generous act, one taboo, one festival

GM usage

  • Use signals in description; let tensions become hooks and clocks

Hooks Generator

Roll or pick to seed a session. Combine a hook with a Location and a Faction.

  • Protect a vulnerable thing (who wants it?)
  • Deliver a thing across danger (who opposes you?)
  • Unmask a liar in plain sight (who is fooled?)
  • Break a deal that hurts someone (what is the price?)
  • Recover a lost thing before a timer fills (who else seeks it?)

Cross‑Links

  • Scene procedure and transitions: Scene & Encounter Structure
  • The core cycle: The Gameplay Loop

Prep Tools & GM Workflow

Table of Contents

  • Prep Philosophy
  • Session Prep Checklist
  • Templates
  • GM Workflow
  • Session Log & Debrief
  • Cross‑Links

Prep Philosophy

Prep what moves play; improvise the rest. Focus on levers you can pull (tags, conditions, clocks, terrain) and on clear stakes. Avoid writing plots; write situations with objectives, pressure, and exits. Tie every prep item to a question you will ask at the table: “What do you do?”

Principles

  • Ready, not rigid: leave space for player solutions
  • Visible state: clocks, tags, and conditions are prepared up front
  • Fail‑forward: plan costs that advance the fiction, not roadblocks
  • Small packets: one page per scene/encounter; link to references

Session Prep Checklist

  • Agenda: recap, goals, timebox, safety check‑in
  • Scenes: 2–4 likely scenes with objective, stakes, and levers
  • Clocks: progress and pressure per scene (sizes 4/6/8)
  • Space: 1–2 tags that matter; how to flip them
  • NPCs: names, goals, leverage; a hook and a weakness each
  • Encounters: roles/ranks/budget; counterplay and terrain synergy
  • Tables: DC ladder cues; conditions/tags quick refs
  • Exits: success/complication outcomes and transitions

Templates

Scene Template

  • Title & Objective
  • Stakes (Full/Partial/Fail); DC cues; Tags
  • Clocks (progress/pressure) with sizes
  • GM Prompts (opening, mid, exit); Exits/Transitions

NPC Template

  • Name, Role, Goal, Leverage
  • Hooks (easy/risky), Weakness, Tag/Condition
  • GM Usage: how they move scenes forward

Encounter Template

  • Roles/Ranks; Budget; Terrain Tags
  • Signature Moves; Counterplay; Behavior Script
  • Clocks and DC cues by lever

Clock Template

  • Name & Type (progress/pressure)
  • Size (4/6/8); Triggers; Clear/Spill conditions

Example — Filled Scene Template

Title & Objective: Market Roof Chase — recover the ledger before the courier escapes.

Stakes

  • Full: you corner the courier on the rooftop and take the ledger
  • Partial: you get the ledger but draw Heat 1 or suffer a minor condition
  • Fail: the courier vanishes into the crowd; Reinforcements +2

DC cues & Tags

  • Maneuver (DC 16) across Slick tiles; Set Up (DC 14) to create a shortcut
  • Tags: Elevated, Slick; create Cover with a vendor’s canopy (Set Up)

Clocks

  • Progress — Courier Cornered (6)
  • Pressure — Heat (6)

GM Prompts

  • Opening: “You spot the courier leap for the next roof — what do you do?”
  • Mid: “Do you press the shortcut or regain footing?”
  • Exit: “With the ledger in hand, do you slip away or chase the accomplice?”

GM Workflow

Before Session

  • Review last log: clocks, tags, conditions, loose hooks
  • Pick 2–3 scenes and 1 set piece; fill checklists/templates
  • Print or lay out quick refs (DC ladder, tags/conditions)

During Session

  • Open with recap; state today’s stakes and timebox
  • Run the loop; pre‑state beats; keep clocks visible
  • Rotate spotlight; keep passes short; close on change
  • On Partial/Fail, move the fiction; offer clear levers

After Session

  • Log what changed (clocks, tags, conditions, resources)
  • Note new hooks, NPC shifts, and lingering risks
  • Set a tentative first scene for next time

Session Log & Debrief

Log Template

  • Date, Session #, Agenda outcome
  • Scene summaries (objective, result, new state)
  • Updated clocks (progress/pressure) and campaign timers
  • NPC changes (goals/leverage), new/cleared tags and conditions
  • Next hooks (A/B options), first scene seed

Debrief Prompts

  • What moved forward? What escalated?
  • Which levers did players use? Which went untouched?
  • What prep paid off? What can be lighter next time?

Cross‑Links

Quick Reference Sheets

Table of Contents

  • DC Ladder & Outcome Tiers
  • Gameplay Loop & Scene Procedure
  • Tags & Conditions
  • Group Checks & Contests
  • Combat Cheat Sheet
  • Rulings Checklist
  • Cross‑Links

DC Ladder & Outcome Tiers

DC cues

  • 12 Easy: safe, aided, trivial with time
  • 14 Routine: standard challenge, normal tools
  • 16 Tough: notable risk, bad angle, poor tools
  • 18 Hard: steep odds, strong opposition, tight window
  • 20 Heroic: exceptional, stacked against, slim margin
  • 22 Legendary: near impossible without setup or luck

Outcome tiers

  • Full: objective achieved cleanly; tick progress or gain position
  • Partial: progress with cost; fill pre‑stated pressure or apply a tag
  • Fail: no progress; escalate danger; reveal a new obstacle or cost
  • Crits: amplify change; consider clearing a small tag on crit success

Gameplay Loop & Scene Procedure

Loop

  • Ask → Declare → Judge → Resolve → Update → Ask
  • Pre‑state stakes; tie fiction to numbers; keep state visible

Scene procedure

  • Frame → Stakes → Check → Narrate → React
  • Name 1–2 tags that matter; show levers to flip them
  • On Partial, move the fiction (tick pressure, apply tag); avoid stalls

Tags & Conditions

Tags (space levers)

  • Dim/Obscuring: favors stealth; hinders navigation or ranged checks
  • Slick/Cramped: hinders forced movement; increases risk of falls
  • Fragile/Solid Cover: degrades on Partial; protects on Full

Conditions (state changes)

  • Exhausted: reduce effectiveness until rest/aid
  • Restrained: limit movement; clear via help, time, or leverage
  • Bleeding: time pressure; clear via first aid or rest

GM usage

  • Add 1–2 meaningful tags per scene; make effects explicit
  • Offer clear ways to clear/mitigate conditions

Group Checks & Contests

Group checks

  • Majority: succeed if most do; Partial if split
  • All‑Must‑Succeed: use when a single failure breaks the attempt
  • Leader‑with‑Help: leader rolls; up to +2 aid dice from helpers

Contests

  • Both sides roll; higher wins; ties are Partial by default
  • Pre‑state results for each side

Combat Cheat Sheet

Ordering

  • Conversational or Popcorn; rotate spotlight; break ties by danger/sense

Core actions

  • Set Up: create angle/space; reduce DCs; apply tags
  • Strike: contest vs defender or passive DC
  • Maneuver: shove, trip, disarm, reposition; trade space/position on Partial
  • Defend/Withdraw: change position/effect; clear a minor tag; break contact

Terrain levers

  • Elevation, Cover (Fragile/Solid), Dim/Obscuring, Slick/Cramped
  • On Partial, degrade cover or tick pressure as telegraphed

Rulings Checklist

  • Say stakes: Full/Partial/Fail before dice
  • Choose DC from fiction; note Advantage/Disadvantage from tags/position
  • Map tier to fiction; move forward on Partial/Fail
  • Update state: tick clocks, add/remove tags, impose/clear conditions
  • Ask again and rotate spotlight

Cross‑Links

  • The core cycle: The Gameplay Loop
  • Scene procedure and transitions: Scene & Encounter Structure
  • Mechanics overview (GM cues): Mechanics Overview
  • Combat ordering and hazards: Combat (GM Guidance)

Solo Play

Table of Contents

  • How Solo Adapts the Loop
  • Solo Scene Procedure
  • Oracles & Prompts
  • Clocks, Tags, Conditions
  • Safety & Scope
  • Worked Mini Example
  • Cross‑Links

How Solo Adapts the Loop

You still use the table loop (Ask → Declare → Judge → Resolve → Update → Ask), but you ask an oracle instead of a GM when you need outside input. Keep a short journal: write questions, answers, and what changed. Prefer visible state (tags, conditions, clocks) over secret notes.

Principles

  • Ask concrete questions (“Does the guard leave?”)
  • Pick odds before rolling (Very Unlikely → Very Likely)
  • Keep results visible: update clocks and note tags/conditions

Solo Scene Procedure

  1. Frame: set objective, name 1–2 tags, state stakes
  2. Ask: when fiction is unclear, ask the oracle; otherwise proceed
  3. Check: pick tool and DC from fiction; pre‑state Full/Partial/Fail
  4. Resolve: roll; interpret tier; update state (clocks/tags/conditions)
  5. Log: write a brief note of what changed and any new hooks
  6. Ask again: choose your next action based on the new state

Oracles & Prompts

Yes/No Oracle (choose odds, then roll 4d6)

  • Very Unlikely: yes on 20+
  • Unlikely: yes on 18+
  • 50/50: yes on 14+
  • Likely: yes on 10+
  • Very Likely: yes on 8+

Note: This uses the standard 4d6 roll (average 14) to determine yes/no outcomes. The thresholds create roughly the odds you’d expect for each category.

Detail Prompts (roll d6 twice or choose)

  • Theme: Debt • Trust • Escape • Intrigue • Mercy • Betrayal
  • Texture: Crowded • Quiet • Rain • Firelight • Gritty • Ornate

GM usage (solo)

  • If a roll suggests trouble, introduce a pressure clock or tag
  • If you need a nudge, pick a prompt and tie it to your current tags/clocks

Clocks, Tags, Conditions

Use the same levers as at the table. Pair progress/pressure clocks (sizes 4/6/8) to pace scenes. Only tick complication clocks on Partial when you’ve pre‑stated them for the scene or beat.

Patterns

  • Full: tick progress; consider clearing a minor tag on crit
  • Partial: tick pre‑stated pressure; add a tag or minor condition
  • Fail: no progress; escalate pressure; reveal a complication

Safety & Scope

Timebox scenes (20–30 minutes). When you feel drift, restate stakes and theme, or end the scene on the next meaningful change. Use lines/veils for tone; avoid dwelling on unwanted content—summarize and move on.

Worked Mini Example

Setup: You search the Sunken Cloister for a reliquary before the tide.

Tags: Dim, Waist‑Deep Water. Clocks: Progress — Reliquary (6); Pressure — Tide (6).

Frame: “Full: find a safe route and advance 2; Partial: advance 1 and Tide 1; Fail: Tide +2 and a minor condition.”

Ask: Is there a safe ledge route? (50/50 → roll 12: Yes)

Check: Survey (DC 16, Tough) to trace carvings under the waterline.

Resolve:

  • Full: Tick Reliquary 2; note a carved fish path
  • Partial: Tick Reliquary 1 and Tide 1; Tag: Off‑Route
  • Fail: No progress; Tide +2; Condition: Soaked or Snagged Strap

Log: “Carved fish marks; progress 1; Tide 1; Off‑Route applied.” Next, ask if a side chamber offers a shortcut (Unlikely).

Cross‑Links

  • Solo concepts (reference): Solo Guide
